class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_(JMSDF)_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_(DDG_173)_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_%28JMSDF%29_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_%28DDG_173%29_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_051115-N-8492C-125_The_Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force_(JMSDF)_destroyer_JDS_Kongou_(DDG_173)_sails_in_formation_with_other_JMSDF_ships_and_ships_assigned_to_the_USS_Kitty_Hawk_Carrier_Strike_Group.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force">JMSDF</a> <a href="/wiki/Kong%C5%8D_class_destroyer" class="mw-redirect" title="Kong\xc5\x8d class destroyer"><i>Kong\xc5\x8d</i> class destroyer</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Japan maintains one of the largest military budgets of any country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The country\'s military (the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Self-Defense_Forces" title="Japan Self-Defense Forces">Japan Self-Defense Forces</a> \xe2\x80\x93 JSDF) is restricted by <a href="/wiki/Article_9_of_the_Japanese_Constitution" title="Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution">Article 9 of the Japanese Constitution</a>, which renounces Japan\'s right to declare war or use military force in international disputes. Accordingly, Japan\'s Self-Defense Forces is an unusual military that has never fired shots outside Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Japan is the highest-ranked Asian country in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">Global Peace Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a> survey published in 2015 ranked Japan as the world\xe2\x80\x99s fourth most-powerful military behind the United States, Russia and China.<sup id="cite_ref-CreditSuisse2015_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CreditSuisse2015-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The military is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Defense (Japan)">Ministry of Defense</a>, and primarily consists of the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Ground_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Ground Self-Defense Force">Japan Ground Self-Defense Force</a> (JGSDF), the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Maritime_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force">Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force</a> (JMSDF) and the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Air_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Air Self-Defense Force">Japan Air Self-Defense Force</a> (JASDF). The Japan Maritime Self-Defense Force (JMSDF) is a regular participant in <a href="/wiki/Exercise_RIMPAC" title="Exercise RIMPAC">RIMPAC</a> maritime exercises.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The forces have been recently used in peacekeeping operations; the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Iraq_Reconstruction_and_Support_Group" title="Japanese Iraq Reconstruction and Support Group">deployment of troops to Iraq</a> marked the first overseas use of Japan\'s military since World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-Iraq_deployment_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iraq_deployment-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Japan_Business_Federation" title="Japan Business Federation">Japan Business Federation</a> has called on the government to lift the ban on arms exports so that Japan can join multinational projects such as the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Strike_Fighter_program" title="Joint Strike Fighter program">Joint Strike Fighter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 21st century is witnessing a rapid change in global power balance along with globalization. The security environment around Japan has become increasingly severe as represented by nuclear and missile development by <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>. Transnational threats grounded on technological progress including international terrorism and cyber attacks are also increasing their significance.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan&#39;s_Security_Policy_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan&#39;s_Security_Policy-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Japan, including its Self-Defense Forces, has contributed to the maximum extent possible to the efforts to maintain and restore international peace and security, such as <a href="/wiki/UN_peacekeeping" class="mw-redirect" title="UN peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping</a> operations. Building on the ongoing efforts as a peaceful state, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Japan" title="Government of Japan">Government of Japan</a> has been making various efforts on its security policy which include: the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Council_(Japan)" title="National Security Council (Japan)">National Security Council</a> (NSC), the adoption of the National Security Strategy (NSS), and the National Defense Program Guidelines (NDPG).<sup id="cite_ref-Japan&#39;s_Security_Policy_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan&#39;s_Security_Policy-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> These efforts are made based on the belief that Japan, as a "Proactive Contributor to Peace", needs to contribute more actively to the peace and stability of the region and the international community, while coordinating with other countries including its ally, the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan&#39;s_Security_Policy_127-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan&#39;s_Security_Policy-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan has close economic and military relations with the United States; the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Mutual_Cooperation_and_Security_between_the_United_States_and_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Mutual Cooperation and Security between the United States and Japan">US-Japan security alliance</a> acts as the cornerstone of the nation\'s foreign policy.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> A member state of the United Nations since 1956, Japan has served as a non-permanent <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> member for a <a href="/wiki/List_of_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council#List_by_number_of_years_as_Security_Council_member" title="List of members of the United Nations Security Council">total of 20 years</a>, most recently for 2009 and 2010. It is one of the <a href="/wiki/G4_nations" title="G4 nations">G4 nations</a> seeking permanent membership in the Security Council.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2014, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Shinz%C5%8D_Abe" title="Shinz\xc5\x8d Abe">Shinz\xc5\x8d Abe</a> said Japan wanted to shed the passiveness it has maintained since the end of World War II and take more responsibility for regional security. He said Japan wanted to play a key role and offered neighboring countries Japan\'s support.<sup id="cite_ref-JapanAsia_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JapanAsia-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, they have been engaged in international <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> operations including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_peacekeeping" title="United Nations peacekeeping">UN peacekeeping</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Recent tensions, particularly with North Korea,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> have reignited the debate over the status of the JSDF and its relation to Japanese society.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> New military guidelines, announced in December 2010, will direct the JSDF away from its <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> focus on the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces" title="Soviet Armed Forces">Soviet Union</a> to a focus on <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People&#39;s Liberation Army">China</a>, especially regarding the territorial dispute over the <a href="/wiki/Senkaku_Islands" title="Senkaku Islands">Senkaku Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MARTIN_FACKLER_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MARTIN_FACKLER-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Japan" title="Economy of Japan">Economy of Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg/220px-Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg/330px-Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg/440px-Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_stock_exchange.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Stock_Exchange" title="Tokyo Stock Exchange">Tokyo Stock Exchange</a>, one of the largest stock exchanges in Asia<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg/220px-Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg/330px-Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg/440px-Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ginza_Wako_Clock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ginza" title="Ginza">Ginza</a>, a luxury shopping area in Tokyo</div></div></div>\n<p>Japan is the third largest national economy in the world, after the United States and China, in terms of <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and the fourth largest national economy in the world, after the United States, China and India, in terms of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Japan\'s <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">public debt</a> was estimated at more than 230 percent of its annual gross domestic product, the largest of any nation in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In August 2011, <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="Moody&#39;s">Moody\'s</a> rating has cut Japan\'s long-term sovereign debt rating one notch from Aa3 to Aa2 inline with the size of the country\'s deficit and borrowing level. The large budget deficits and government debt since the 2009 global recession and followed by the earthquake and tsunami in March 2011 caused the rating downgrade.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service sector</a> accounts for three quarters of the gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan has a large industrial capacity, and is home to some of the largest and most technologically advanced producers of motor vehicles, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machine_tool" title="Machine tool">machine tools</a>, steel and nonferrous metals, ships, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">chemical substances</a>, textiles, and <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processed foods</a>. <a href="/wiki/Agriculture,_forestry,_and_fishing_in_Japan" title="Agriculture, forestry, and fishing in Japan">Agricultural businesses in Japan</a> cultivate 13 percent of Japan\'s land, and Japan accounts for nearly 15 percent of the global fish catch, second only to China.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Japan\'s labor force consisted of some 65.9 million workers.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Japan has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_unemployment_rate" title="List of countries by unemployment rate">low unemployment rate</a> of around four percent. Some 20 million people, around 17 per cent of the population, were below the poverty line in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Housing_in_Japan" title="Housing in Japan">Housing in Japan</a> is characterized by limited land supply in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan\'s exports amounted to US$4,210 per capita in 2005. As of  2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Japan\'s main export markets were the United States (20.2 percent), China (17.5 percent), South Korea (7.1 percent), Hong Kong (5.6 percent) and Thailand (4.5 percent). Its main exports are transportation equipment, motor vehicles, iron and steel products, semiconductors and auto parts.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Japan\'s main import markets as of  2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> were China (24.8 percent), the United States (10.5 percent), Australia (5.4 percent) and South Korea (4.1 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan\'s main imports are machinery and equipment, <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>, foodstuffs (in particular beef), chemicals, textiles and raw materials for its industries. By market share measures, domestic markets are the least open of any <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a> country.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd2008_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd2008-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Junichir%C5%8D_Koizumi" class="mw-redirect" title="Junichir\xc5\x8d Koizumi">Junichir\xc5\x8d Koizumi</a>\'s administration began some pro-competition reforms, and foreign investment in Japan has soared.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan ranks 34th of 190 countries in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">ease of doing business index</a> and has <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_tax_revenue_as_percentage_of_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by tax revenue as percentage of GDP">one of the smallest tax revenues</a> of the developed world. The Japanese variant of capitalism has many distinct features: <a href="/wiki/Keiretsu" title="Keiretsu">keiretsu</a> enterprises are influential, and <a href="/wiki/Permanent_employment" title="Permanent employment">lifetime employment</a> and seniority-based career advancement are relatively common in the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_work_environment" title="Japanese work environment">Japanese work environment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-oecd2008_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oecd2008-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Japanese companies are known for management methods like "<a href="/wiki/The_Toyota_Way" title="The Toyota Way">The Toyota Way</a>", and <a href="/wiki/Shareholder_activism" class="mw-redirect" title="Shareholder activism">shareholder activism</a> is rare.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Japan\'s top global brands include <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canon_Inc." title="Canon Inc.">Canon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_UFJ_Financial_Group" title="Mitsubishi UFJ Financial Group">Mitsubishi UFJ (MUFG)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uniqlo" title="Uniqlo">Uniqlo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lexus" title="Lexus">Lexus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subaru" title="Subaru">Subaru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridgestone" title="Bridgestone">Bridgestone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suzuki" title="Suzuki">Suzuki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_history">Economic history</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Japan" title="Economic history of Japan">Economic history of Japan</a></div>\n<p>Modern Japan\'s economic growth began in the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">Edo period</a>. Some of the surviving elements of the Edo period are <a href="/wiki/Kaid%C5%8D" title="Kaid\xc5\x8d">roads</a> and water transportation routes, as well as financial instruments such as <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures contracts</a>, banking and insurance of the <a href="/wiki/Osaka_rice_brokers" class="mw-redirect" title="Osaka rice brokers">Osaka rice brokers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> During the Meiji period from 1868, Japan expanded economically with the embrace of the <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Many of today\'s enterprises were founded at the time, and Japan emerged as the most developed nation in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The period of overall real economic growth from the 1960s to the 1980s has been called the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_post-war_economic_miracle" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese post-war economic miracle">Japanese post-war economic miracle</a>: it averaged 7.5 percent in the 1960s and 1970s, and 3.2 percent in the 1980s and early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Growth slowed in the 1990s during the <a href="/wiki/Lost_Decade_(Japan)" title="Lost Decade (Japan)">"Lost Decade"</a> due to after-effects of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_asset_price_bubble" title="Japanese asset price bubble">Japanese asset price bubble</a> and government policies intended to wring speculative excesses from the stock and real estate markets. Efforts to revive economic growth were unsuccessful and further hampered by the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">global slowdown in 2000</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The economy recovered after 2005; GDP growth for that year was 2.8 percent, surpassing the growth rates of the US and <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, Japan ranks highly for <a href="/wiki/Competitiveness" class="mw-redirect" title="Competitiveness">competitiveness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a>. It is ranked sixth in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a> for 2015\xe2\x80\x932016.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_fishery">Agriculture and fishery</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture,_forestry,_and_fishing_in_Japan" title="Agriculture, forestry, and fishing in Japan">Agriculture, forestry, and fishing in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu,_Japan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/220px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/330px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG/440px-Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu%2C_Japan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rice_Paddies_In_Aizu,_Japan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Rice_paddy" class="mw-redirect" title="Rice paddy">rice paddy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aizu" title="Aizu">Aizu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Prefecture" title="Fukushima Prefecture">Fukushima Prefecture</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Japanese agricultural sector accounts for about 1.4% of the total country\'s GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan_Country_Report_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_Country_Report-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Only 12% of Japan\'s land is suitable for cultivation.<sup id="cite_ref-As_Farmers_Age,_Japan_Rethinks_Relationship_With_Food,_Fields_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-As_Farmers_Age,_Japan_Rethinks_Relationship_With_Food,_Fields-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trip_Report_-_Japan_Agricultural_Situation_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trip_Report_-_Japan_Agricultural_Situation-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Due to this lack of arable land, a system of terraces is used to farm in small areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Urbanites_Help_Sustain_Japan&#39;s_Historic_Rice_Paddy_Terraces_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Urbanites_Help_Sustain_Japan&#39;s_Historic_Rice_Paddy_Terraces-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> This results in one of the world\'s highest levels of crop yields per unit area, with an overall agricultural self-sufficiency rate of about 50% on fewer than 56,000 square kilometres (14,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">acres</a>) cultivated.\n</p><p>Japan\'s small agricultural sector, however, is also highly subsidized and protected, with government regulations that favor small-scale cultivation instead of large-scale agriculture as practiced in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-As_Farmers_Age,_Japan_Rethinks_Relationship_With_Food,_Fields_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-As_Farmers_Age,_Japan_Rethinks_Relationship_With_Food,_Fields-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> There has been a growing concern about farming as the current farmers are aging with a difficult time finding successors.<sup id="cite_ref-How_will_Japan&#39;s_farms_survive?_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_will_Japan&#39;s_farms_survive?-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rice accounts for almost all of Japan\'s cereal production.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan_-_Agriculture_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_-_Agriculture-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Japan is the second-largest agricultural product importer in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan_-_Agriculture_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_-_Agriculture-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Rice, the most protected crop, is subject to tariffs of 777.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-Trip_Report_-_Japan_Agricultural_Situation_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trip_Report_-_Japan_Agricultural_Situation-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-With_fewer,_bigger_plots_and_fewer_part-time_farmers,_agriculture_could_compete_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-With_fewer,_bigger_plots_and_fewer_part-time_farmers,_agriculture_could_compete-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1996, Japan ranked fourth in the world in <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_by_country" title="Fishing industry by country">tonnage of fish caught</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_review_of_fisheries_and_aquaculture_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_review_of_fisheries_and_aquaculture-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Japan captured 4,074,580 metric tons of fish in 2005, down from 4,987,703 tons in 2000, 9,558,615 tons in 1990, 9,864,422 tons in 1980, 8,520,397 tons in 1970, 5,583,796 tons in 1960 and 2,881,855 tons in 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-Fish_capture_by_country_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fish_capture_by_country-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, the total aquaculture production was predicted at 1,301,437 tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan_National_Aquaculture_Sector_Overview_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_National_Aquaculture_Sector_Overview-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Japan\'s total fisheries production was 4,762,469 fish.<sup id="cite_ref-World_fisheries_production,_by_capture_and_aquaculture,_by_country_(2010)_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_fisheries_production,_by_capture_and_aquaculture,_by_country_(2010)-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Offshore fisheries accounted for an average of 50% of the nation\'s total fish catches in the late 1980s although they experienced repeated ups and downs during that period.\n</p><p>Today, Japan maintains one of the world\'s largest fishing fleets and accounts for nearly 15% of the global catch,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> prompting some claims that Japan\'s fishing is leading to depletion in fish stocks such as <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_tribunal_halts_Japanese_tuna_over-fishing_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_tribunal_halts_Japanese_tuna_over-fishing-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Japan has also sparked controversy by supporting quasi-commercial <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Japan" title="Whaling in Japan">whaling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Japanese_whaling_&#39;science&#39;_rapped_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japanese_whaling_&#39;science&#39;_rapped-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_in_Japan" title="Manufacturing in Japan">Manufacturing in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg/220px-Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg/330px-Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg/440px-Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toyota_Plant_Ohira_Sendai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Toyota factory in <a href="/wiki/Ohira,_Miyagi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohira, Miyagi">Ohira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">Miyagi Prefecture</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Japan\'s industrial sector makes up approximately 27.5% of its GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Japan\'s major industries are motor vehicles, electronics, machine tools, metals, ships, chemicals and processed foods; some major Japanese industrial companies include <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canon_Inc." title="Canon Inc.">Canon Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">Toshiba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Steel_%26_Sumitomo_Metal" title="Nippon Steel &amp; Sumitomo Metal">Nippon Steel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan is the third largest automobile producer in the world, and is home to <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, the world\'s largest automobile company.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The Japanese consumer electronics industry, once considered the strongest in the world, is currently in a state of decline as competition arises in countries like <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> However, despite also facing similar competition from South Korea and China, the Japanese shipbuilding industry is expected to remain strong due to an increased focus on specialized, high-tech designs.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trade_and_services_in_Japan" title="Trade and services in Japan">Trade and services in Japan</a></div>\n<p>Japan\'s service sector accounts for about three-quarters of its total economic output.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan_Country_Report_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_Country_Report-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Banking, insurance, real estate, retailing, <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in Japan">transportation</a>, and telecommunications are all major industries, with companies such as <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_UFJ_Financial_Group" title="Mitsubishi UFJ Financial Group">Mitsubishi UFJ</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mizuho_Financial_Group" title="Mizuho Financial Group">Mizuho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Telegraph_and_Telephone" title="Nippon Telegraph and Telephone">NTT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Electric_Power_Company" title="Tokyo Electric Power Company">TEPCO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nomura_Holdings" title="Nomura Holdings">Nomura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Estate_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Mitsubishi Estate Co.">Mitsubishi Estate</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%86ON_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x86ON (company)">\xc3\x86ON</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsui_Sumitomo_Insurance" class="mw-redirect" title="Mitsui Sumitomo Insurance">Mitsui Sumitomo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Softbank" class="mw-redirect" title="Softbank">Softbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Japan_Railway_Company" title="East Japan Railway Company">JR East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seven_%26_I_Holdings_Co." title="Seven &amp; I Holdings Co.">Seven &amp; I</a>, <a href="/wiki/KDDI" title="KDDI">KDDI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a> listed as some of the largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_Global_500_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_Global_500-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Four of the five <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_the_world_by_circulation" class="mw-redirect" title="List of newspapers in the world by circulation">most circulated newspapers in the world</a> are <a href="/wiki/Japanese_newspapers" title="Japanese newspapers">Japanese newspapers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Newspapers_Total_Circulation_2011_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Newspapers_Total_Circulation_2011-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Japan_Post_Holdings" title="Japan Post Holdings">Japan Post Holdings</a>, one of the country\'s largest providers of savings and insurance services, was slated for privatization by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Japan_govt_aims_to_list_Japan_Post_in_three_years_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_govt_aims_to_list_Japan_Post_in_three_years-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The six major <a href="/wiki/Keiretsu" title="Keiretsu">keiretsus</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sumitomo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sumitomo">Sumitomo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuyo" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuyo">Fuyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsui" title="Mitsui">Mitsui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dai-Ichi_Kangyo" class="mw-redirect" title="Dai-Ichi Kangyo">Dai-Ichi Kangyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanwa_Group" title="Sanwa Group">Sanwa</a> Groups.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Japan" title="Tourism in Japan">Tourism in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg/220px-Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg/330px-Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg/440px-Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5004" data-file-height="3336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chuurei-tou_Fujiyoshida_17025277650_c59733d6ba_o.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Fuji" title="Mount Fuji">Mount Fuji</a>, the highest peak, is considered as one of the most iconic <a href="/wiki/Landmark" title="Landmark">landmarks</a> of Japan.</div></div></div>\n<p>Japan attracted 19.73 million international tourists in 2015<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> and increased by 21.8% to attract 24.03 million international tourists in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Tourism from abroad is one of the few promising businesses in Japan. Foreign visitors to Japan doubled in last decade and reached 10 million people for the first time in 2013, led by increase of Asian visitors.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg/220px-KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg/330px-KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg/440px-KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KyotoFushimiInariLarge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fushimi_Inari-taisha" title="Fushimi Inari-taisha">Fushimi Inari-taisha</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kyoto" title="Kyoto">Kyoto</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2008, the Japanese government has set up Japan Tourism Agency and set the initial goal to increase foreign visitors to 20 million in 2020. In 2016, having met the 20 million target, the government has revised up its target to 40 million by 2020 and to 60 million by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Number_of_Foreign_Visitors_Surpassed_20_million_(Japan)_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Number_of_Foreign_Visitors_Surpassed_20_million_(Japan)-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan has 20 <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Himeji_Castle" title="Himeji Castle">Himeji Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Historic_Monuments_of_Ancient_Kyoto_(Kyoto,_Uji_and_Otsu_Cities)" title="Historic Monuments of Ancient Kyoto (Kyoto, Uji and Otsu Cities)">Historic Monuments of Ancient Kyoto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Historic_Monuments_of_Ancient_Nara" title="Historic Monuments of Ancient Nara">Nara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Popular tourist attractions include <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Tokyo" title="Tourism in Tokyo">Tokyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">Hiroshima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Fuji" title="Mount Fuji">Mount Fuji</a>, ski resorts such as <a href="/wiki/Niseko" class="mw-redirect" title="Niseko">Niseko</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Prefecture" title="Okinawa Prefecture">Okinawa</a>, riding the <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">shinkansen</a> and taking advantage of Japan\'s <a href="/wiki/Ryokan_(Japanese_inn)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ryokan (Japanese inn)">hotel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Onsen" title="Onsen">hotspring</a> network.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg/220px-Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg/330px-Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg/440px-Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Himeji_sakura01_adjusted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cherry_blossom" title="Cherry blossom">Cherry blossom</a> with <a href="/wiki/Himeji_Castle" title="Himeji Castle">Himeji Castle</a> in the background, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>For inbound tourism, Japan was <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">ranked</a> 16th in the world in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-WTO_Tourism_Highlights_2015_Edition_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTO_Tourism_Highlights_2015_Edition-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, the <i><a href="/wiki/Yomiuri_Shimbun" title="Yomiuri Shimbun">Yomiuri Shimbun</a></i> published a modern list of famous sights under the name <i><a href="/wiki/Heisei_Hyakkei" class="mw-redirect" title="Heisei Hyakkei">Heisei Hyakkei</a></i> (the Hundred Views of the Heisei period). The <i><a href="/wiki/Travel_and_Tourism_Competitiveness_Report" title="Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report">Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report</a> 2017</i> ranks Japan 4th out of 141 countries overall, which was the best in Asia. Japan gained relatively high scores in almost all aspects, especially health and hygiene, safety and security, cultural resources and business travel.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG/220px-The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG/330px-The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG/440px-The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_A-Bomb_Dome_and_oyster_boat_%22Kanawa%22%EF%BC%882015.08.22%EF%BC%89.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Memorial" title="Hiroshima Peace Memorial">Hiroshima Peace Memorial</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2016, 24,039,053 foreign tourists visited Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Neighbouring South Korea is Japan\'s most important source of foreign tourists. In 2010, the 2.4 million arrivals made up 27% of the tourists visiting Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-Dickie_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dickie-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Chinese travelers are the highest spenders in Japan by country, spending an estimated 196.4 billion yen (US$2.4 billion) in 2011, or almost a quarter of total expenditure by foreign visitors, according to data from the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Tourism_Agency" title="Japan Tourism Agency">Japan Tourism Agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Japanese government hopes to receive 40 million foreign tourists every year by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-10year_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10year-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, 28,690,900 foreign tourists visited Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Japan" title="Science and technology in Japan">Science and technology in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_%282%29.jpg/220px-HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_%282%29.jpg/330px-HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_%282%29.jpg/440px-HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HTV-6_grappled_by_the_International_Space_Station%27s_robotic_arm_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kounotori_6" title="Kounotori 6">Kounotori 6</a> grappled by the International Space Station\'s robotic arm</div></div></div>\n<p>Japan is a leading nation in <a href="/wiki/Scientific_research" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific research">scientific research</a>, particularly in fields related to the natural sciences and engineering. The country ranks second among the most innovative countries in the <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Innovation_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Bloomberg Innovation Index">Bloomberg Innovation Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Nearly 700,000 researchers share a US$130 billion <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> budget.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The amount spent on <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> relative to gross domestic product is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_research_and_development_spending" title="List of countries by research and development spending">third highest in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> The country is a world leader in <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_research" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundamental research">fundamental scientific research</a>, having produced twenty-two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel laureates</a> in either physics, chemistry or medicine<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> and three <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields medalists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japanese scientists and engineers have contributed to the advancement of agricultural sciences, electronics, <a href="/wiki/Industrial_robot" title="Industrial robot">industrial robotics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optics" title="Optics">optics</a>, chemicals, <a href="/wiki/Semiconductor" title="Semiconductor">semiconductors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Life_science" class="mw-redirect" title="Life science">life sciences</a> and various fields of engineering. Japan leads the world in <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a> production and use, possessing more than 20% (300,000 of 1.3 million) of the world\'s industrial robots as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94though its share was historically even higher, representing one-half of all industrial robots worldwide in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Japan boasts the third highest number of scientists, technicians, and engineers per capita in the world with 83 scientists, technicians and engineers per 10,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronics_and_automotive_engineering">Electronics and automotive engineering</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry_in_Japan" title="Electronics industry in Japan">Electronics industry in Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Japan" title="Automotive industry in Japan">Automotive industry in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/220px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/330px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg/440px-2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5019" data-file-height="2492" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_Toyota_Camry_TRD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A plug-in <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid car</a> manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, one of the world\'s largest carmakers\xe2\x80\x94Japan is the third-largest maker of automobiles in the world<sup id="cite_ref-:0_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The Japanese electronics and automotive manufacturing industry is well known throughout the world, and the country\'s electronic and automotive products account for a large share in the global market, compared to a majority of other countries. Brands such as <a href="/wiki/Fujifilm" title="Fujifilm">Fujifilm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canon_Inc." title="Canon Inc.">Canon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> are internationally famous. It is estimated that 16% of the world\'s gold and 22% of the world\'s silver is contained in Japanese electronics.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aerospace">Aerospace</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/220px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/330px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg/440px-Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2039" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kibo_PM_and_ELM-PS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Experiment Module">Japanese Experiment Module</a> (Kibo) at the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Aerospace_Exploration_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency">Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency</a> (JAXA) is Japan\'s national <a href="/wiki/Space_agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Space agency">space agency</a>; it conducts space, planetary, and aviation research, and leads development of rockets and satellites. It is a participant in the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Experiment Module">Japanese Experiment Module</a> (Kibo) was added to the station during <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> assembly flights in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">space probe</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Akatsuki_(spacecraft)" title="Akatsuki (spacecraft)">Akatsuki</a></i> was launched May 20, 2010, and achieved orbit around Venus on December 9, 2015. Japan\'s plans in <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> include: developing the <i><a href="/wiki/Mercury_Magnetospheric_Orbiter" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercury Magnetospheric Orbiter">Mercury Magnetospheric Orbiter</a></i> to be launched in 2018;<sup id="cite_ref-FACTS_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FACTS-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> and building a <a href="/wiki/Colonization_of_the_Moon" title="Colonization of the Moon">moon base</a> by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 14, 2007, it launched lunar explorer <a href="/wiki/SELENE" title="SELENE">SELENE</a> (Selenological and Engineering Explorer) on a <a href="/wiki/H-IIA" title="H-IIA">H-IIA</a> (Model H2A2022) carrier rocket from <a href="/wiki/Tanegashima_Space_Center" title="Tanegashima Space Center">Tanegashima Space Center</a>. SELENE is also known as Kaguya, after the lunar princess of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_the_Bamboo_Cutter" title="The Tale of the Bamboo Cutter">The Tale of the Bamboo Cutter</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-jaxa_nickname_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaxa_nickname-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Kaguya is the largest lunar mission since the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo program</a>. Its purpose is to gather data on the <a href="/wiki/Moon#Formation" title="Moon">moon\'s origin and evolution</a>. It entered a lunar orbit on October 4,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> flying at an altitude of about 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The probe\'s mission was ended when it was deliberately crashed by JAXA into the Moon on June 11, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_laureates">Nobel laureates</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Japanese_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Japanese Nobel laureates">List of Japanese Nobel laureates</a></div>\n<p>Japan has received the most science <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prizes</a> in Asia and ranked 8th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Yukawa" title="Hideki Yukawa">Hideki Yukawa</a>, educated at <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_University" title="Kyoto University">Kyoto University</a>, was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">prize in physics</a> in 1949. <a href="/wiki/Shin%27ichir%C5%8D_Tomonaga" title="Shin&#39;ichir\xc5\x8d Tomonaga">Shin\'ichir\xc5\x8d Tomonaga</a> followed in 1965. Solid-state physicist <a href="/wiki/Leo_Esaki" title="Leo Esaki">Leo Esaki</a>, educated at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">University of Tokyo</a>, received the prize in 1973. <a href="/wiki/Kenichi_Fukui" title="Kenichi Fukui">Kenichi Fukui</a> of Kyoto University shared the 1981 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">prize in chemistry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Susumu_Tonegawa" title="Susumu Tonegawa">Susumu Tonegawa</a>, also educated at Kyoto University, became Japan\'s first laureate in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">physiology or medicine</a> in 1987. Japanese chemists took prizes in 2000 and 2001: first <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Shirakawa" title="Hideki Shirakawa">Hideki Shirakawa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Institute_of_Technology" title="Tokyo Institute of Technology">Tokyo Institute of Technology</a>) and then <a href="/wiki/Ry%C5%8Dji_Noyori" title="Ry\xc5\x8dji Noyori">Ry\xc5\x8dji Noyori</a> (Kyoto University). In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Masatoshi_Koshiba" title="Masatoshi Koshiba">Masatoshi Koshiba</a> (University of Tokyo) and <a href="/wiki/Koichi_Tanaka" title="Koichi Tanaka">Koichi Tanaka</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tohoku_University" title="Tohoku University">Tohoku University</a>) won in physics and chemistry, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Makoto_Kobayashi_(physicist)" title="Makoto Kobayashi (physicist)">Makoto Kobayashi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toshihide_Masukawa" class="mw-redirect" title="Toshihide Masukawa">Toshihide Masukawa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yoichiro_Nambu" title="Yoichiro Nambu">Yoichiro Nambu</a>, who was an American citizen when awarded, shared the physics prize and <a href="/wiki/Osamu_Shimomura" title="Osamu Shimomura">Osamu Shimomura</a> also won the chemistry prize in 2008. <a href="/wiki/Isamu_Akasaki" title="Isamu Akasaki">Isamu Akasaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiroshi_Amano" title="Hiroshi Amano">Hiroshi Amano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shuji_Nakamura" title="Shuji Nakamura">Shuji Nakamura</a>, who is an American citizen when awarded, shared the physics prize in 2014 and the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Yoshinori_Ohsumi" title="Yoshinori Ohsumi">Yoshinori Ohsumi</a> in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Japan" title="Transport in Japan">Transport in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Japan_Airlines,_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_(19455285040).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/220px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/330px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg/440px-Japan_Airlines%2C_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_%2819455285040%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4678" data-file-height="3120" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Japan_Airlines,_Boeing_787-9_JA861J_NRT_(19455285040).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> of Japan</div></div></div>\n<p>Japan\'s road spending has been extensive.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Its 1.2&#160;million kilometres (0.75&#160;million miles) of paved road are the main means of transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> As of April 2012, Japan has approximately 1,215,000 kilometres (755,000 miles) of roads made up of 1,022,000 kilometres (635,000 miles) of city, town and village roads, 129,000 kilometres (80,000 miles) of prefectural roads, 55,000 kilometres (34,000 miles) of general national highways and 8,050 kilometres (5,000 miles) of national <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Japan" title="Expressways of Japan">expressways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> A single network of high-speed, divided, limited-access <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll roads</a> connects major cities on <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shikoku" title="Shikoku">Shikoku</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a> has a separate network, and <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Island" title="Okinawa Island">Okinawa Island</a> has a highway of this type. A single network of high-speed, divided, limited-access <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">toll roads</a> connects major cities and is operated by toll-collecting enterprises. New and used cars are inexpensive; car ownership fees and fuel levies are used to promote energy efficiency. However, at just 50 percent of all distance traveled, car usage is the lowest of all G8 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-transtatsjp_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transtatsjp-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since privatisation in 1987, <a href="/wiki/List_of_railway_companies_in_Japan" title="List of railway companies in Japan">dozens of Japanese railway companies</a> compete in regional and local passenger transportation markets; major companies include seven <a href="/wiki/Japan_Railways_Group" title="Japan Railways Group">JR</a> enterprises, <a href="/wiki/Kintetsu_Railway" title="Kintetsu Railway">Kintetsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seibu_Railway" title="Seibu Railway">Seibu Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keio_Corporation" title="Keio Corporation">Keio Corporation</a>. Some 250 high-speed <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">Shinkansen</a> trains connect major cities and Japanese trains are known for their safety and punctuality.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Proposals for a new <a href="/wiki/JR%E2%80%93Maglev" class="mw-redirect" title="JR\xe2\x80\x93Maglev">Maglev</a> route between Tokyo and Osaka are at an advanced stage.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are 175 airports in Japan;<sup id="cite_ref-cia_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> the largest domestic airport, <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">Haneda Airport</a>, is <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by passenger traffic">Asia\'s second-busiest airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> The largest international gateways are <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Narita International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansai_International_Airport" title="Kansai International Airport">Kansai International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%ABbu_Centrair_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Ch\xc5\xabbu Centrair International Airport">Ch\xc5\xabbu Centrair International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nagoya_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Nagoya Port">Nagoya Port</a> is the country\'s largest and busiest port, accounting for 10 percent of Japan\'s trade value.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Japan" title="Energy in Japan">Energy in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_(8388173865).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/220px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/330px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg/440px-Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_%288388173865%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2808" data-file-height="2132" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_04780017_(8388173865).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kashiwazaki-Kariwa_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Kashiwazaki-Kariwa Nuclear Power Plant">Kashiwazaki-Kariwa Nuclear Power Plant</a>, a nuclear plant with seven units, the largest single nuclear power station in the world</div></div></div>\n<p>As of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 46.1% of energy in Japan was produced from petroleum, 21.3% from coal, 21.4% from natural gas, 4.0% from <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Japan" title="Nuclear power in Japan">nuclear power</a> and 3.3% from <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>. Nuclear power produced 9.2 percent of Japan\'s electricity, as of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, down from 24.9 percent the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> However, by May 2012 all of the country\'s nuclear power plants had been taken offline because of ongoing public opposition following the <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster</a> in March 2011, though government officials continued to try to sway public opinion in favor of returning at least some of Japan\'s 50 nuclear reactors to service.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> As of  November 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Japan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, two reactors at Sendai are likely to restart in early 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Japan lacks significant domestic reserves and so has a heavy dependence on <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_imports" title="List of countries by oil imports">imported energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Japan has therefore aimed to diversify its sources and maintain high levels of energy efficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Japan" title="Water supply and sanitation in Japan">Water supply and sanitation in Japan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg/220px-Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg/330px-Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg/440px-Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1707" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokuyama_Dam_under_involved_construction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tokuyama_Dam" title="Tokuyama Dam">Tokuyama Dam</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gifu_Prefecture" title="Gifu Prefecture">Gifu Prefecture</a> is the largest dam in Japan</div></div></div>\n<p>The government took responsibility for regulating the water and sanitation sector is shared between the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health,_Labour_and_Welfare_(Japan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Health, Labour and Welfare (Japan)">Ministry of Health, Labor and Welfare</a> in charge of water supply for domestic use; the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Land,_Infrastructure,_Transport_and_Tourism_(Japan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism (Japan)">Ministry of Land, Infrastructure, Transport and Tourism</a> in charge of water resources development as well as sanitation; the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Environment_(Japan)" title="Ministry of the Environment (Japan)">Ministry of the Environment</a> in charge of ambient water quality and environmental preservation; and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs_and_Communications" title="Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications">Ministry of Internal Affairs and Communications</a> in charge of performance benchmarking of utilities.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Access to an <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water source</a> is universal in Japan. 97% of the population receives piped water supply from public utilities and 3% receive water from their own wells or unregulated small systems, mainly in rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics of Japan">Demographics of Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">Japanese people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Japan" title="Ethnic groups of Japan">Ethnic groups of Japan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Japan" title="List of metropolitan areas in Japan">List of metropolitan areas in Japan</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg/220px-Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg/330px-Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg/440px-Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="507" data-file-height="338" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bjs48_02_Ainu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ainu_people" title="Ainu people">Ainu</a>, an ethnic minority people from Japan</div></div></div>\n<p>Japan\'s population is estimated at around 128 million,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> with 80% of the population living on <a href="/wiki/Honsh%C5%AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Honsh\xc5\xab">Honsh\xc5\xab</a>. Japanese society is <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistically</a>, ethnically and culturally homogeneous,<sup id="cite_ref-MulticulturalJapan_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MulticulturalJapan-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gentensei_Shinko_Shinbun_2010_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gentensei_Shinko_Shinbun_2010-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> composed of 98.5% ethnic Japanese,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> with small populations of foreign workers.<sup id="cite_ref-MulticulturalJapan_235-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MulticulturalJapan-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Koreans_in_Japan" title="Koreans in Japan">Zainichi Koreans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Japan" title="Chinese people in Japan">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Japan" title="Filipinos in Japan">Filipinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian people">Brazilians</a> mostly <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Brazilian">of Japanese descent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nikkeijin_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikkeijin-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peruvian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Peruvian people">Peruvians</a> mostly <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Peruvian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Peruvian">of Japanese descent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Americans_in_Japan" title="Americans in Japan">Americans</a> are among the small minority groups in Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, there were about 134,700 non-Latin American Western (not including more than 33,000 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Forces_Japan" title="United States Forces Japan">American military personnel</a> and their dependents stationed throughout the country)<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> and 345,500 <a href="/wiki/Latin_Americans" title="Latin Americans">Latin American</a> expatriates, 274,700 of whom were <a href="/wiki/Brazilians_in_Japan" title="Brazilians in Japan">Brazilians</a> (said to be primarily Japanese descendants, or <i><a href="/wiki/Nikkeijin" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikkeijin">nikkeijin</a></i>, along with their spouses),<sup id="cite_ref-nikkeijin_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nikkeijin-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> the largest community of Westerners.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The most dominant native ethnic group is the <a href="/wiki/Yamato_people" title="Yamato people">Yamato people</a>; primary minority groups include the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Ainu_people" title="Ainu people">Ainu</a><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ryukyuan_people" title="Ryukyuan people">Ryukyuan peoples</a>, as well as social minority groups like the <i><a href="/wiki/Burakumin" title="Burakumin">burakumin</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> There are persons of mixed ancestry incorporated among the Yamato, such as those from <a href="/wiki/Bonin_Islands" title="Bonin Islands">Ogasawara Archipelago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mccormack1999_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mccormack1999-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, foreign-born non-naturalized workers made up only 1.5% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Japan is widely regarded as ethnically homogeneous, and does not compile ethnicity or race statistics for Japanese nationals; sources varies regarding such claim, with at least one analysis describing Japan as a <a href="/wiki/Multiethnic_society" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiethnic society">multiethnic society</a><sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> while another analysis put the number of Japanese nationals of recent <a href="/wiki/H%C4%81fu" title="H\xc4\x81fu">foreign descent</a> to be minimal.<sup id="cite_ref-Gentensei_Shinko_Shinbun_2010_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gentensei_Shinko_Shinbun_2010-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Most Japanese continue to see Japan as a <a href="/wiki/Monoculturalism" title="Monoculturalism">monocultural society</a>.
